‚óŹ Review complete. All three high-effort passes came back clean on the
  substantive axes:

  - Reuse: _chain_line shares scaffolding with dashed_line but the duplication
  is justified (4-phase chain vs 2-phase dash) and matches the file's
  small-standalone-primitive style; merging would churn dashed_line's 3 callers
  for no behavior gain. _draw_x_cross remains the single chokepoint ‚ÄĒ no
  parallel path. No change.
  - Efficiency: _chain_line is O(segments) with O(1) per-segment work,
  direction/length computed once, no per-pixel work, guaranteed to terminate
  (pos strictly increases). ~‚Č§288 tiny draw.line calls per canvas worst case ‚ÄĒ
  negligible vs. the grid's existing dashed lines. No change.
  - Quality: correct and an improvement; the _draw_x_cross 2-tuple loop is
  cleaner than two duplicated calls; comments are genuine WHY; no dead code.

  Two nits fixed (in _chain_line):
  1. Renamed params long/short ‚Üí long_dash/short_dash (former Py2 keyword; reads
  as a length now).
  2. Documented the constants/contract in the docstring: the dash rhythm is a
  deliberate fixed-pixel cadence (not TILE_SIZE-relative, since it's a drawing
  convention), and all lengths must be positive so the march always advances ‚ÄĒ
  closing the latent "all-zero lengths would hang" concern without adding a
  runtime guard inconsistent with dashed_line.

  Verified: syntax OK, generation runs clean.

  Searched for 2 patterns, read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ The small empty bbox is a column that was placed, then visually erased by a 
  later draw, but survived the orphan scrub because of how the scrub samples
  pixels.

  Here's the exact sequence in generate_image (generate_column.py:1866-1939):

  1. Column placed and labelled (line¬†1918). Gate (_spot_is_clear +
  struct_rects) ensures the spot was clear at placement time.
  2. Six unchecked drawers then run over the same canvas (none of them consult
  col_rects):
    - draw_internal_partitions (1924) ‚ÄĒ thin partition lines between column
  faces
    - draw_extra_bubbles (1927) ‚ÄĒ extra circles
    - draw_filled_triangle_markers (1930) ‚ÄĒ north-arrow / dim-arrow filled 
  triangles (the arrows you can see in your screenshot)
    - draw_slab_signs (1933) ‚ÄĒ text cards
    - draw_empty_intersection_decoys (1935) ‚ÄĒ text at empty intersections
    - draw_grid_crossing_decoys (1936) ‚ÄĒ short T/+ line decoys
  3. Orphan scrub (1939) ‚ÄĒ _is_orphan_label samples only 5 pixels: centre + the
  4 outline mid-points (line 632-653). It drops the label only if ALL 5 are
  paper-background (‚Č•235 each channel).

  The failure mode: one of those late drawers (most likely a triangle marker /
  dim arrow, since you can see arrows next to that bbox) plants ink that happens
  to clip one of the 5 sample pixels ‚ÄĒ even just an arrow-tip stroke grazing
  one outline midpoint is enough. The scrub then sees "at least one dark sample
  ‚Üí not an orphan" and keeps the label, even though the column's body itself has
  been overpainted. From a distance the bbox looks empty because the only ink
  inside it is a tiny stray fragment from the overdrawer.

  Why the scrub can't catch this: 5 points is too sparse to certify "no column
  underneath." Any stray dark pixel ‚ÄĒ partition line, arrow stroke, decoy line,
  text letter ‚ÄĒ anywhere on those 5 coordinates defeats it. The drawing-order
  assumption ("nothing draws over a column") is what the scrub relies on, and
  that assumption silently breaks for those 6 functions.

  The fix, if you want one, is either: (a) make those 6 late drawers consult
  col_rects/col_bboxes and skip column footprints (proper fix), or (b) tighten
  the orphan scrub ‚ÄĒ sample a denser grid inside the bbox and require >X% to be
  ink, not just "any one pixel" (cheap fix). Want me to implement either?

‚úĽ Worked for 2m 54s

‚ÄĽ recap: Goal: produce clean YOLO column-detection training tiles via generate_column.py. Current task: diagnosed why a labelled bbox appears over blank space ‚ÄĒ six post-column drawers don't check column footprints and the 5-point orphan scrub is too sparse. Next: await your call on which fix to implement. (disable recaps in /config)

‚ĚĮ what is the orphan scrub, can we remove it entirely                           

‚óŹ What it is (generate_column.py:632-653, called at 1939):

  labels = [lbl for lbl in labels if not _is_orphan_label(lbl, pixels)]

  A post-draw filter that walks every YOLO label and asks: "is there actually 
  any column ink inside this bbox, or is it sitting on blank paper?" It samples
  5 pixels ‚ÄĒ centre + 4 outline mid-points just inside the column edge ‚ÄĒ and
  drops the label if all 5 are ‚Č•235 RGB (paper white). It's a safety net for one
  specific failure: a column was placed, then a later draw refilled its body
  with background, leaving the label pointing at nothing.

  Can it be removed?

  Technically yes, but it's the only thing currently catching three real failure
  modes:

  1. Late drawers overpainting columns ‚ÄĒ the 6 functions between line 1918 and
  1939 (draw_internal_partitions, draw_extra_bubbles,
  draw_filled_triangle_markers, draw_slab_signs, draw_empty_intersection_decoys,
  draw_grid_crossing_decoys) don't consult col_rects. Without the scrub,
  anything they erase becomes a labelled-but-blank bbox ‚Üí the model learns
  "blank patches are columns."
  2. Structure X-cross / interior clears ‚ÄĒ _draw_hollow_core clears the cavity
  to background. If any column label ever ends up inside a cavity (the footprint
  registration in col_rects is supposed to prevent this), the scrub is the
  second line of defence.
  3. Edge columns at tile borders ‚ÄĒ when a column's centre is just inside a
  tile, most of the column body may sit outside; if the in-tile portion is bg,
  the scrub drops it.

  Removing it without replacing it would put noisy "no-column-here" labels back
  into the dataset ‚ÄĒ exactly the problem we've been hunting down in the
  human-check tiles.

  The cleaner alternative is to make removal safe by routing every late drawer
  through a col_rects-aware gate (skip if the draw would overlap a column
  footprint). That eliminates failure mode #1 at the source, and _bay_is_clear /
  the structure-footprint registration already covers #2. Then the scrub
  becomes redundant and can be deleted.

  Want me to do that ‚ÄĒ gate the 6 late drawers on col_rects and then drop
  _is_orphan_label?

‚ĚĮ   labels = [lbl for lbl in labels if not _is_orphan_label(lbl, pixels)]       
                                                                                
    A post-draw filter that walks every YOLO label and asks: "is there actually 
  any column ink inside this bbox, or is it sitting on blank paper?" It         
  samples 5 pixels ‚ÄĒ centre + 4 outline mid-points just inside                  
    the column edge ‚ÄĒ and drops the label if all 5 are ‚Č•235 RGB (paper white).  
  It's a safety net for one specific failure: a column was placed, then a later

    label pointing at nothing  if there is such a check, but empty bbox still

‚óŹ You're right ‚ÄĒ and it's not a bug, it's the design being too lenient. Here's
  exactly why it failed for that bbox:

  The scrub's rule is: drop the label only if ALL 5 sample pixels are 
  background. If even ONE of the 5 lands on any dark pixel ‚ÄĒ for any reason ‚ÄĒ it
  says "not orphan, keep it." Look at the predicate (line 650):

  return _all_background(pixels, (...))   # ALL must be bg

  So a single stray ink pixel hitting one of the 5 sample coordinates is enough
  to defeat the whole check. And there is plenty of stray ink near that bbox in
  your screenshot:

  - An arrow shaft / triangle edge clipping one outline mid-point
  - A partition line (draw_internal_partitions) terminating exactly at the
  column's face ‚ÄĒ by design it lands on the outline pixel the scrub samples
  - A grid-crossing decoy line passing through one sample point
  - Bubble outline grazing a sample point
  - A slab-sign / decoy text letter touching a sample

  Any one of those keeps the label. The scrub does fire ‚ÄĒ but only on the
  cleanest overdraws (e.g., a wide white text card whose background swamps all 5
  points). The messy overdraws ‚ÄĒ arrows, single thin lines, line endings ‚ÄĒ slip
  through, and that's what you're seeing.

  There are two ways to make it actually work:

  1. Make the scrub stricter ‚ÄĒ sample a dense grid inside the bbox (say 7√ó7 = 49
  points) and drop the label if e.g. >85% are background. A lone stray pixel no
  longer saves it.
  2. Fix it at the source ‚ÄĒ gate the 6 late drawers (draw_internal_partitions,
  draw_extra_bubbles, draw_filled_triangle_markers, draw_slab_signs,
  draw_empty_intersection_decoys, draw_grid_crossing_decoys) on col_rects so
  nothing is allowed to draw over a column in the first place. Then the scrub
  isn't needed and can be deleted.

  Option 2 is the real fix (root cause); option 1 is a tighter safety net. Want
  me to do (2)?

     ‚Ēā def _text_aabb(font, text, cx, cy):                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     """Pixel AABB of `text` centred at (cx, cy). Uses font.getbbox      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (Pillow                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     ‚Č•9.2); falls back to font.getsize for older Pillow ‚ÄĒ matches the    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā dual-path                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     pattern already in _text_centered."""                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     try:                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         x1, y1, x2, y2 = font.getbbox(text)                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         tw, th = x2 - x1, y2 - y1                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     except AttributeError:                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         tw, th = font.getsize(text)                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     return (int(cx - tw / 2), int(cy - th / 2),                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā             int(cx + tw / 2), int(cy + th / 2))                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Used by the three text-emitting drawers (partition labels, slab signs,  ‚Ēā

‚óŹ You're right ‚ÄĒ I had the wrong frame. I was reading that screenshot as a

  inference time. The small bbox in blank space is a false positive, not a
  labelling artifact.

  That completely changes the diagnosis. The orphan-scrub / late-drawer-gating

  and an FP from the trained model is a model-behaviour / training-data-coverage
  problem.

  Before I rewrite the plan let me make sure I understand what you want:

‚óŹ¬†User answered Claude's questions:
  ‚éŅ ¬†¬∑ What's the goal ‚ÄĒ diagnose why the model fires at that empty spot, or 
     change the training data so it stops? ‚Üí Diagnose only (no edits)
     ¬∑ How was the inference run that produced this screenshot done? ‚Üí Full A0 
     plan tiled with overlap

‚óŹ Diagnosis only. With full A0 tiled at 1280 / 200 px overlap, the FP next to a
  real column has three plausible causes ‚ÄĒ ranked by how well they match the
  screenshot:

  1. Tile-seam ghost (most likely given "beside the real column")

  The 200 px overlap means every column near a tile boundary is seen by two
  tiles. Each tile independently predicts the column. The merge step (whatever
  your inference does ‚ÄĒ sahi, YOLO's built-in tiled inference, or a custom
  union+NMS) is supposed to dedupe across tiles, but:

  - The two predictions usually have slightly different bboxes (the model "sees"
  the column differently when it's centred vs. near the edge ‚ÄĒ edge crops are
  partial context, so the predicted box can shrink, shift, or rotate the aspect
  ratio).
  - Global NMS uses IoU; if the displaced ghost has IoU < 0.5 with the canonical
  detection, NMS keeps both.
  - The ghost is then a small displaced box right next to the real one ‚ÄĒ exactly
  your screenshot.

  This is by far the commonest FP pattern in tiled inference, and is independent
  of training data quality. You can't train it away ‚ÄĒ it's a
  post-processing/NMS issue. The fix lives in the inference path, not
  generate_column.py. Common remedies (for context, not for now): increase NMS
  IoU to ~0.3, or use a "merge if any-overlap > X" rule across tile boundaries
  instead of plain IoU NMS.

  2. Sliver self-FP from the "centre-in-tile" rule

  The synthetic dataset's _save_tiles (generate_column.py:1735) labels a column
  only if its centre is inside the tile. A column straddling a tile edge appears
  in two tiles:
  - In tile A (centre inside): full bbox extending past the right edge ‚Üí
  labelled.
  - In tile B (centre outside): just a sliver near the left edge ‚Üí unlabelled.

  So the model is trained on partial slivers as negatives. At inference on a
  real plan, a small ambiguous dark fragment near a tile edge (text, arrow tail,
  partial wall corner) can match the "labelled fragment from the other tile's
  perspective" pattern and fire. Result: a small bbox in apparent blank space
  near a tile boundary.

  If the small FP in your screenshot is close to where a tile seam would land on
  the A0 canvas (every 1080 px in your grid), this is the cause. The position
  of the small bbox relative to the tile grid is the tell.

  3. Context-shortcut FP

  The visible arrow in the screenshot is suggestive. The training data has
  draw_filled_triangle_markers (north arrows) but NOT dimension arrows that
  flank columns the way real construction drawings do. If real plans
  systematically put a leader/dim arrow pattern adjacent to columns, the model
  can learn arrow-cluster ‚áí column nearby as a shortcut and fire on a blank
  patch that's flanked by similar arrows. The synthetic decoys
  (draw_empty_intersection_decoys) only counter the text-near-empty-intersection
  shortcut, not the arrow-near-empty-intersection one.

  How to tell which one it is:
  - Open the source plan at full resolution. Note the pixel coordinates of the
  small FP bbox.
  - Check whether (fp_x mod 1080) is close to 0 or close to 1080 (= near a tile
  seam) ‚Üí cause #1 or #2.
  - If it's not near a seam, look at what surrounds it in a ~150 px window. If
  it's near dim-arrow / leader-line clutter resembling other columns'
  annotation, it's cause #3.
  - If running inference with conf=0.25 (YOLO default), try conf=0.4. If the FP
  disappears, it was a borderline confidence call and any of the three are
  plausible ‚ÄĒ just under-trained.

  Nothing to edit. Want me to write a small offline check that, given the source
  plan and the prediction JSON, classifies each FP into seam-ghost / sliver /
  context ‚ÄĒ so you can see the distribution before deciding whether to chase #2
  (training-data) or #1 (post-processing)?

‚úĽ Crunched for 1m 36s

‚ĚĮ do you recommend post-processing over training-data?                          

‚óŹ Yes ‚ÄĒ start with post-processing.

  Why: The most likely cause (seam ghost) is fundamentally a post-processing
  problem ‚ÄĒ the model is right both times, the merge step is what's failing.
  Training-data tweaks can't eliminate it. Post-processing also iterates in
  seconds (no retrain), is tunable per-deployment, and you've said you train
  manually, so the retrain loop is the slowest thing in this workflow.

  Tradeoff: Post-processing masks symptoms but can't fix a model that's
  genuinely confused. If a large fraction of your FPs turn out to be cause #3
  (context shortcut, e.g. "arrow cluster ‚áí column"), no NMS tweak will save you
  and you'd be paying for retrains you avoided. So the order I'd recommend is:
  (a) post-processing first for the seam/sliver bulk, (b) measure what's left,
  (c) only then invest in synthetic-data coverage for whatever residue remains.

‚úĽ Brewed for 16s

‚ÄĽ recap: You're diagnosing a false-positive empty bbox in the trained model's predictions on a real A0 plan; we agreed post-processing first (fix cross-tile NMS), training-data work only if FPs remain. Next: identify whether the FP sits near a tile seam. (disable recaps in /config)

‚óŹ Let me first classify what each FP teaches us, then ask scope.

  Cat 1 ‚ÄĒ "bbox becomes a line in text detection": very tall-narrow or very
  wide-flat aspect ratios over text strokes. Real columns are square-to-2:1; the
  model is emitting 4:1+ predictions. This is a clean post-processing win ‚ÄĒ
  reject any detection with aspect > ~2.5:1.

  Cat 2 ‚ÄĒ letter "B" in H-RCB1 detected as column (Image #2): monospace "B" has
  two stacked rectangles ‚Üí a tiny outlined-square pattern. The synthetic data
  does have text decoys (draw_empty_intersection_decoys, draw_slab_signs,
  ROOM_LABEL_POOL) but they're at much larger sizes than B-sized characters, and
  never specifically place letters with column-mimicking glyph shapes (B / D /
  O / 0 / 8) adjacent to walls. Training-data problem ‚ÄĒ text patterns
  under-represented at column-pixel sizes.

  Cat 3 ‚ÄĒ FPs along stair edge / inside stair (Image #3): the synthetic stair
  (maybe_draw_stair_3wall) currently places edge-flanking columns along each of
  its three walls (per the dense-flanking policy: max_cols=5, per-edge ~0.70).
  The model correctly generalised: "vertical strip of stair-edge ‚áí many small
  columns." Real stairs don't have flanking columns on every step. The vertical
  strip of FPs in Image #3 is exactly the pattern we taught. User-stated fix:
  reduce stair flanking density (the user wrote this explicitly). Same logic
  likely applies to lift and opening ‚ÄĒ drop the flanking probability/cap, or
  move flanking only to the CORNERS, not along the long walls.

  Cat 4 ‚ÄĒ multiple overlapping FPs on vertical text labels "RCB3" / "RS1" (Image
  #4): vertical text labels (rotated 90¬į) repeat dense vertical strokes that
  the model sees as a column row. Same root cause as Cat 2 (text
  under-represented), made worse by lack of rotated/vertical text in synthetic
  data. Also exacerbated by overlapping tile detections not being deduped
  (post-processing). Mostly training-data, partly post-processing.

  Summary:

     ‚Ēā Plan ‚ÄĒ Combined fix for the four real-plan FP categories                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā produced four                                                           ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Cat: 1                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Symptom: Detection is a thin line over text strokes                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Image: ‚ÄĒ                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Root cause: Model emits high-aspect bboxes; no aspect filter at         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā inference                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Cat: 2                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Symptom: Letter inside a beam label (e.g. "B" in H-RCB1) detected as    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā column                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Image: #2                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Root cause: Synthetic text decoys are oversized and never               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   letter-shape-mimic-a-column                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Cat: 3                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Symptom: Dense vertical strip of FPs along a real stair's edge          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Image: #3                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Root cause: Synthetic stair drops up to 12 flanking columns per stair   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (long                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   edges max_cols=6 √ó 2, plus corners), teaching "stair edge ‚áí many      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā columns"                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Cat: 4                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Symptom: Multiple overlapping FPs on vertical text labels RCB3, RS1     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Image: #4                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Root cause: Rotated text under-represented in training; cross-tile NMS  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā too                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   lenient                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā User direction (this conversation):                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Combined plan covering all four.                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Stair flanking: total 1‚Äď3 columns per stair, never dense.             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - Existing user constraint (carries over): training is done by the user ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā manually; this plan only edits generation + adds a post-processing      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā script.                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Approach                                                                ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā half                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā of Cat¬†4. Not wired into this repo's training; CLAUDE.md notes          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā "deployed                                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā artifact consumed by downstream tooling" ‚ÄĒ same pattern.                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Reused, not reinvented:                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - _bbox_overlaps_any (generate_column.py:588) ‚ÄĒ gates all new decoy     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā placements against col_rects so decoys never overlap real columns.      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - _padded_rect (:584) ‚ÄĒ pad candidate decoy rects before the overlap    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā test.                                                                   ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā draw_internal_partitions for vertical wall-thickness labels. Reuse for  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā new                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā rotated text decoys, no new primitive.                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - _place_edge_flanking_columns (:1055) ‚ÄĒ keep unchanged; the stair      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā change                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā is at the caller (caps the total budget, not the helper).               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Edits                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā A. generate_column.py ‚ÄĒ Cat 3: thin stair flanking                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā maybe_draw_stair_3wall (:1203), the per-stair flanking block currently  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā at                                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā :1306-1316:                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā # CURRENT (dense):                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā long_names = (("left","right") if sh >= sw else ("top","bottom"))       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā for name, ex1, ey1, ex2, ey2, dx, dy in _outer_edges(sx1, sy1, sx2,     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā sy2):                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     edge_prob, edge_max = ((1.0, 6) if name in long_names else (0.5,    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 2))                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     if random.random() > edge_prob: continue                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     labels.extend(_place_edge_flanking_columns(..., max_cols=edge_max)) ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Replace with a total per-stair budget of 1‚Äď3 columns, distributed       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā across                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā edges (not per-edge multiplied):                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā # NEW (sparse):                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā # Real stairs rarely have flanking columns; never drop a dense strip.   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Budget                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā # the WHOLE stair to 1‚Äď3 columns total, sprinkled across at most 1‚Äď2    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā edges so                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā # the model never learns "stair edge ‚áí vertical column row".            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā budget = random.randint(1, 3)                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā edges  = list(_outer_edges(sx1, sy1, sx2, sy2))                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā random.shuffle(edges)                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā for name, ex1, ey1, ex2, ey2, dx, dy in edges:                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     if budget <= 0: break                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     take = random.randint(1, min(2, budget))     # ‚Č§2 cols on any       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā single edge                                                             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     placed = _place_edge_flanking_columns(                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         draw, ex1, ey1, ex2, ey2, dx, dy, col_rects, max_cols=take)     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     labels.extend(placed)                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     budget -= len(placed)                                               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Keep the corner T/+ columns from _place_outer_corner_tp_columns(:1303)  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ÄĒ                                                                       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā those teach legitimate corner-column-at-stair patterns and the FP       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā screenshot                                                              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā isn't at stair corners.                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Lift (:1413, max_cols=5) and opening (:1194, max_cols=4) flanking stay  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā unchanged for now ‚ÄĒ user only flagged stairs. Note in the plan for      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā future:                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā same treatment may be needed if FPs appear at lift/opening edges later. ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā B. generate_column.py ‚ÄĒ Cat 2 + Cat 4: column-sized text decoys         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The existing text decoys (draw_empty_intersection_decoys :1623,         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā draw_slab_signs :1612, WALL_THICK_POOL / ROOM_LABEL_POOL in             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā partitions) are drawn at the annotation reference size                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (ann_sz_ref = max(20, TILE_SIZE // 53) ‚Čą 24 px). That's too large to    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā look                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā like a column. The model is firing on text rendered at column-pixel     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā sizes                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (letters that are ~12‚Äď30 px tall and column-shaped like B/D/O/0/8/H/R)  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ‚ÄĒ these                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā do not exist in the training data.                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Add ONE new drawer draw_small_text_decoys (placed near draw_slab_signs, ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā ~`:1610`). Pattern:                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā COLUMN_MIMIC_GLYPH_POOL = list("BDOQ08HRC1IL")   # glyphs that match    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā shaded                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                    # square / unshaded  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā outline                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                    # / round / T-shape  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā columns                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā COLUMN_MIMIC_TOKEN_POOL = ["B","D","O","8","H","R","C2","RS1","RCB3",   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                             "C1","H-C2","T1","T2","RC","CW","CL"]       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā # Sizes chosen to span the column class size range so the decoys land   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā on the                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā # same activations the model uses for columns. See ranges at module     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā top.                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā def draw_small_text_decoys(draw, v_lines, h_lines, col_rects, gc):      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     """Drop ~10‚Äď25 small text fragments (single letters, short tokens,  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     rotated tokens) at column-mimicking pixel sizes scattered across    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā the                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     canvas ‚ÄĒ NOT labelled as columns. Trains the model to suppress      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā text-as-                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     column FPs (Cat 2 and Cat 4 from the real-plan run)."""             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     if random.random() > 0.85 or len(v_lines) < 2 or len(h_lines) < 2:  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         return                                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     n = random.randint(10, 25)                                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     for _ in range(n):                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         sz   = random.randint(14, 28)            # ‚Čą unshaded column    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā side                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         font = _load_regular_font(sz)                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         text = random.choice(COLUMN_MIMIC_TOKEN_POOL)                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         # Anywhere on the canvas except right at the bubble margin      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         cx = random.randint(120, IMG_WIDTH  - 120)                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         cy = random.randint(120, IMG_HEIGHT - 120)                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         rotated = random.random() < 0.40                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         cand_w, cand_h = (sz, sz) if rotated else (sz * len(text), sz)  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         cand = (cx - cand_w//2, cy - cand_h//2,                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                 cx + cand_w//2, cy + cand_h//2)                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         if _bbox_overlaps_any(cand, col_rects):                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā             continue                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         if rotated:                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā             _paste_rotated_text(img, cx, cy, text, font, gc, angle=90)  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā         else:                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā             _text_centered(draw, cx, cy, text, gc, font)                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (Note: this needs img in scope ‚ÄĒ pass it from generate_image. Mirrors   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā how draw_internal_partitions already receives img for the same reason.) ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Call from generate_image after draw_slab_signs (~`:1933`):              ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā draw_small_text_decoys(draw, v_lines, h_lines, col_rects, gc)           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā This is the single most important Cat 2/4 fix ‚ÄĒ the model has never     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā been                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā told that small column-sized letters / vertical "RCB3" labels are not   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā columns.                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā C. scripts/postprocess_detections.py ‚ÄĒ Cat 1 + Cat 4 residual           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā New standalone script the downstream tooling imports. Two filters:      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā """Post-process YOLO column detections on a tiled-inference output. Two ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā filters, both shape-based (no model needed):                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   (1) Aspect-ratio filter ‚ÄĒ drop detections with max(w,h)/min(w,h) >    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā 2.5.                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā       Real columns are square-to-2:1. Anything taller-than-3√ó is text.  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā   (2) Cross-tile merge ‚ÄĒ IoU-aware NMS across the full canvas at        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā iou_thr=0.30                                                            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā       (looser than YOLO's default 0.50) so the seam-ghost               ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā half-overlapping                                                        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā       duplicate (small displaced bbox next to a real column) gets       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā merged.                                                                 ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Usage:                                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     from scripts.postprocess_detections import filter_detections        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā     detections = filter_detections(detections,                          ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                     max_aspect=2.5, nms_iou=0.30)       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā """                                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Implementation: standard NMS (sort by confidence, greedy IoU            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā suppression),                                                           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā plus a pre-filter on aspect ratio. ~60 lines, no heavyweight deps       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā (numpy +                                                                ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā nothing else). Sketched as a module so the consumer imports it; not     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā wired                                                                   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā into this repo's training scripts.                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā D. No changes to the orphan scrub (revised stance)                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā The earlier plan iteration proposed deleting _is_orphan_label. Drop     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā that                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā work ‚ÄĒ the FPs in question come from inference-time model output on     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā real                                                                    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā plans, not from the synthetic dataset's label-on-blank-paper issue. The ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā orphan scrub is unrelated to these four categories. Leave it.           ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Reused, not reinvented                                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - _bbox_overlaps_any / _padded_rect (:584-602) ‚ÄĒ already the chokepoint ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā used by structure footprint registration and the column gate. Re-used   ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā by                                                                      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā draw_small_text_decoys for the decoy-vs-column overlap test.            ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - _paste_rotated_text (:251) ‚ÄĒ re-used for rotated decoys, no new       ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā rotation primitive.                                                     ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - _text_centered (:427) ‚ÄĒ re-used for non-rotated decoy placement.      ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - _load_regular_font (:230) ‚ÄĒ same font path as existing decoys.        ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - _place_edge_flanking_columns (:1055) ‚ÄĒ unchanged; stair fix is the    ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā caller's budget logic, not the helper.                                  ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā                                                                         ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā Files modified                                                          ‚Ēā

     ‚Ēā other pools at :181-204 + one call line in generate_image).             ‚Ēā
     ‚Ēā - scripts/postprocess_detections.py ‚ÄĒ new file, ~60 lines.              ‚Ēā

‚óŹ Plan rejected ‚ÄĒ new issue surfaced. The user reports unshaded round columns 
  are not being detected (false negative). Let me check what classes exist for
  round/unshaded combinations.

  Searched for 1 pattern, read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

‚óŹ Diagnosis of the unshaded-round FN, then I'll add it to the plan as Cat 5.

  Why cls 4 (unshaded round) is missed:

  1. Severely under-represented. Class weight is 6 out of 126 = ~5% of the main
  grid loop's column draws. With ~30-40 intersections per canvas √ó 50 canvases √ó
  5% ‚Čą 250 cls-4 examples total ‚ÄĒ vs ~13,000 for cls 0 (filled square). The
  model barely sees it. (generate_column.py:1904)
  2. Locked out of every "near-structure" role. _pick_tp_class_and_size
  (:979-990) is explicitly restricted to cls 0/1/2 ‚ÄĒ comment says "structure
  corners on real plans are nearly always filled." That means unshaded circles
  never appear:
    - at stair / lift / opening corners (_place_outer_corner_tp_columns)
    - edge-flanking any structure (_place_edge_flanking_columns via the same
  picker)
    - at core corners (maybe_draw_core_with_corner_columns does its own draw,
  but the picker is shared logic)

  Real plans put unshaded round columns in those positions, so the model has 0
  examples of "unshaded circle adjacent to a stair / core / wall." When it sees
  one at inference, it has no learned response ‚ÄĒ FN.
  3. Fixed 2-px stroke. _make_unshaded (:385-391) hard-codes max(2, lw) = 2 px.
  Real plans have variable stroke weights (1 px / 2 px / 3 px depending on
  drawing scale). At cls 4's 24-42 px size, the outline IS the entire signal ‚ÄĒ a
  stroke-weight mismatch is fatal.
  4. No interior content. Real unshaded round columns often have a small label
  inside the circle (√ė1130, 1130 CIS, class tag). Synthetic cls 4 circles are
  empty. The model has only learned "empty ring = column," which it must
  reconcile with "empty ring = also could be bubble outline" ‚ÄĒ and bubbles are
  negative.
  5. Confusable with axis bubbles. draw_bubble and draw_extra_bubbles draw
  circles with letters inside, often at sizes overlapping cls 4's range. The
  model sees vastly more bubble-circles than column-circles ‚Üí defaults to
  "circle = bubble (suppress)."

  This is the FN root cause. Let me fold it into the combined plan as Cat 5.

     Plan ‚ÄĒ Combined fix for the four real-plan FP categories

     Context

     Real-plan inference (full A0 tiled at 1280 px / 200 px overlap) produced
     four
     distinct false-positive patterns the user catalogued:

     Cat: 1
     Symptom: Detection is a thin line over text strokes (FP)
     Image: ‚ÄĒ
     Root cause: Model emits high-aspect bboxes; no aspect filter at inference
     ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
     Cat: 2
     Symptom: Letter inside a beam label (e.g. "B" in H-RCB1) detected as column

       (FP)
     Image: #2
     Root cause: Synthetic text decoys are oversized and never
       letter-shape-mimic-a-column
     ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
     Cat: 3
     Symptom: Dense vertical strip of FPs along a real stair's edge (FP)
     Image: #3
     Root cause: Synthetic stair drops up to 12 flanking columns per stair (long

       edges max_cols=6 √ó 2, plus corners), teaching "stair edge ‚áí many columns"
     ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
     Cat: 4
     Symptom: Multiple overlapping FPs on vertical text labels RCB3, RS1 (FP)
     Image: #4
     Root cause: Rotated text under-represented in training; cross-tile NMS too
       lenient
     ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ
     Cat: 5
     Symptom: Unshaded round columns (cls 4) not detected (FN)
     Image: user report
     Root cause: (i) 5% weight in grid loop only; (ii) excluded from every
       structure-adjacent role by _pick_tp_class_and_size cls 0/1/2 restriction
       (:983-985); (iii) fixed 2-px stroke; (iv) no interior text; (v)
     confusable
       with the much more numerous axis-bubble circles

     User direction (this conversation):
     - Combined plan covering all five.
     - Stair flanking: total 1‚Äď3 columns per stair, never dense.
     - Existing user constraint (carries over): training is done by the user
     manually; this plan only edits generation + adds a post-processing script.

     Approach

     Two deliverables ‚ÄĒ kept separate because they ship in different paths:

     1. generate_column.py ‚ÄĒ training-data fixes for Cat 2, Cat 3, Cat¬†4.
     2. scripts/postprocess_detections.py (new) ‚ÄĒ standalone post-processing
     filter the downstream tooling can import. Covers Cat 1 + the residual half
     of Cat¬†4. Not wired into this repo's training; CLAUDE.md notes "deployed
     artifact consumed by downstream tooling" ‚ÄĒ same pattern.

     Reused, not reinvented:
     - _bbox_overlaps_any (generate_column.py:588) ‚ÄĒ gates all new decoy
     placements against col_rects so decoys never overlap real columns.
     - _padded_rect (:584) ‚ÄĒ pad candidate decoy rects before the overlap test.
     - _load_regular_font (:230) ‚ÄĒ same font path the existing text decoys use.
     - _paste_rotated_text (:251) ‚ÄĒ already supports angle=90; used by
     draw_internal_partitions for vertical wall-thickness labels. Reuse for new
     rotated text decoys, no new primitive.
     - _place_edge_flanking_columns (:1055) ‚ÄĒ keep unchanged; the stair change
     is at the caller (caps the total budget, not the helper).

     Edits

     A. generate_column.py ‚ÄĒ Cat 3: thin stair flanking

     maybe_draw_stair_3wall (:1203), the per-stair flanking block currently at
     :1306-1316:

     # CURRENT (dense):
     long_names = (("left","right") if sh >= sw else ("top","bottom"))
     for name, ex1, ey1, ex2, ey2, dx, dy in _outer_edges(sx1, sy1, sx2, sy2):
         edge_prob, edge_max = ((1.0, 6) if name in long_names else (0.5, 2))
         if random.random() > edge_prob: continue
         labels.extend(_place_edge_flanking_columns(..., max_cols=edge_max))

     Replace with a total per-stair budget of 1‚Äď3 columns, distributed across
     edges (not per-edge multiplied):

     # NEW (sparse):
     # Real stairs rarely have flanking columns; never drop a dense strip. 
     Budget
     # the WHOLE stair to 1‚Äď3 columns total, sprinkled across at most 1‚Äď2 edges 
     so
     # the model never learns "stair edge ‚áí vertical column row".
     budget = random.randint(1, 3)
     edges  = list(_outer_edges(sx1, sy1, sx2, sy2))
     random.shuffle(edges)
     for name, ex1, ey1, ex2, ey2, dx, dy in edges:
         if budget <= 0: break
         take = random.randint(1, min(2, budget))     # ‚Č§2 cols on any single 
     edge
         placed = _place_edge_flanking_columns(
             draw, ex1, ey1, ex2, ey2, dx, dy, col_rects, max_cols=take)
         labels.extend(placed)
         budget -= len(placed)

     Keep the corner T/+ columns from _place_outer_corner_tp_columns(:1303) ‚ÄĒ
     those teach legitimate corner-column-at-stair patterns and the FP
     screenshot
     isn't at stair corners.

     Lift (:1413, max_cols=5) and opening (:1194, max_cols=4) flanking stay
     unchanged for now ‚ÄĒ user only flagged stairs. Note in the plan for future:
     same treatment may be needed if FPs appear at lift/opening edges later.

     B. generate_column.py ‚ÄĒ Cat 2 + Cat 4: column-sized text decoys

     The existing text decoys (draw_empty_intersection_decoys :1623,
     draw_slab_signs :1612, WALL_THICK_POOL / ROOM_LABEL_POOL in
     partitions) are drawn at the annotation reference size
     (ann_sz_ref = max(20, TILE_SIZE // 53) ‚Čą 24 px). That's too large to look
     like a column. The model is firing on text rendered at column-pixel sizes
     (letters that are ~12‚Äď30 px tall and column-shaped like B/D/O/0/8/H/R) ‚ÄĒ
     these
     do not exist in the training data.

     Add ONE new drawer draw_small_text_decoys (placed near draw_slab_signs,
     ~`:1610`). Pattern:

     COLUMN_MIMIC_GLYPH_POOL = list("BDOQ08HRC1IL")   # glyphs that match shaded
                                                        # square / unshaded 
     outline
                                                        # / round / T-shape 
     columns
     COLUMN_MIMIC_TOKEN_POOL = ["B","D","O","8","H","R","C2","RS1","RCB3",
                                 "C1","H-C2","T1","T2","RC","CW","CL"]
     # Sizes chosen to span the column class size range so the decoys land on 
     the
     # same activations the model uses for columns. See ranges at module top.

     def draw_small_text_decoys(draw, v_lines, h_lines, col_rects, gc):
         """Drop ~10‚Äď25 small text fragments (single letters, short tokens,
         rotated tokens) at column-mimicking pixel sizes scattered across the
         canvas ‚ÄĒ NOT labelled as columns. Trains the model to suppress text-as-
         column FPs (Cat 2 and Cat 4 from the real-plan run)."""
         if random.random() > 0.85 or len(v_lines) < 2 or len(h_lines) < 2:
             return
         n = random.randint(10, 25)
         for _ in range(n):
             sz   = random.randint(14, 28)            # ‚Čą unshaded column side
             font = _load_regular_font(sz)
             text = random.choice(COLUMN_MIMIC_TOKEN_POOL)
             # Anywhere on the canvas except right at the bubble margin
             cx = random.randint(120, IMG_WIDTH  - 120)
             cy = random.randint(120, IMG_HEIGHT - 120)
             rotated = random.random() < 0.40
             cand_w, cand_h = (sz, sz) if rotated else (sz * len(text), sz)
             cand = (cx - cand_w//2, cy - cand_h//2,
                     cx + cand_w//2, cy + cand_h//2)
             if _bbox_overlaps_any(cand, col_rects):
                 continue
             if rotated:
                 _paste_rotated_text(img, cx, cy, text, font, gc, angle=90)
             else:
                 _text_centered(draw, cx, cy, text, gc, font)

     (Note: this needs img in scope ‚ÄĒ pass it from generate_image. Mirrors
     how draw_internal_partitions already receives img for the same reason.)

     Call from generate_image after draw_slab_signs (~`:1933`):

     draw_small_text_decoys(draw, v_lines, h_lines, col_rects, gc)

     This is the single most important Cat 2/4 fix ‚ÄĒ the model has never been
     told that small column-sized letters / vertical "RCB3" labels are not
     columns.

     C. generate_column.py ‚ÄĒ Cat 5: lift the unshaded-round FN

     Five small changes, each addressing a distinct cause:

     (i) Bump the grid-loop weight for cls 4 (:1904-1905):

     # CURRENT:  weights=[65,30,6,9,6,7,3]    # cls 0..6
     # NEW:      weights=[55,28,6,8,15,7,3]   # ~2.5√ó cls 4 share, drawn from
     #                                          cls 0/1 to keep total at 122
     Quintuples cls 4's per-canvas count from ~5 to ~12; brings the absolute
     count
     into the same order of magnitude as the FN floor (a few hundred examples).

     (ii) Allow cls 4 in _pick_tp_class_and_size (:979-990):

     # CURRENT:  cls = random.choices([0,1,2], weights=[70,22,8])[0]
     # NEW:      cls = random.choices([0,1,2,4], weights=[60,20,8,12])[0]
     #           if cls == 4: return cls, random.randint(ROUND_MIN_SIZE, 
     ROUND_MAX_SIZE)
     This is the single largest lever ‚ÄĒ it puts unshaded rounds at stair
     corners, opening corners, lift corners, core corners, AND in every edge-
     flanking call. Update the docstring to remove the "structure corners are
     nearly always filled" claim. Keep cls 5/6 out of TP roles (the user has not
     flagged unshaded square FNs).

     (iii) Vary the unshaded stroke weight in _make_unshaded (:385-391):

     # CURRENT:  return fn(draw, cx, cy, s, (255,255,255), outline, max(2, lw))
     # NEW:
     def _make_unshaded(fn):
         def _draw(draw, cx, cy, s, _fill, outline, lw):
             # Real plans have variable line weights at different drawing 
     scales.
             # Fixed 2-px stroke trained the model on a single weight, missing
             # real unshaded round columns drawn at 1 px or 3 px. See Cat 5.
             w = random.choice([1, 2, 2, 3])
             return fn(draw, cx, cy, s, (255,255,255), outline, w)
         return _draw

     (iv) Optional interior text inside cls 4 ‚ÄĒ add to place_column (:467)
     just after the cls-4 case is drawn:

     # After: bbox, _ = _SHAPE[shape_name](draw, cx, cy, size, fill, outline, 2)
     if cls == 4 and random.random() < 0.55 and size >= 28:
         txt = random.choice(["√ė1130", "1130", "RC", "√ė", "C2", "1130 CIS"])
         sz  = max(8, size // 3)
         _text_centered(draw, cx, cy, txt, (40,40,40), _load_regular_font(sz))
     55% of cls 4 columns now carry a small label, mirroring real-plan practice.
     Teaches "circle + interior text" can also be a column ‚ÄĒ disambiguates from
     empty-ring decoy patterns.

     (v) Separate cls 4 from bubbles by size band: draw_extra_bubbles
     (:1547) uses bubble radius br shared with the axis-bubble code. Confirm
     br is well above ROUND_MAX_SIZE/2 (i.e. extra bubbles are visibly larger
     than cls 4 columns). If not, clamp extra-bubble radius to >= ROUND_MAX_SIZE
     so the size distributions don't overlap. This is a one-line check, no edit
     unless the overlap exists.

     D. scripts/postprocess_detections.py ‚ÄĒ Cat 1 + Cat 4 residual

     New standalone script the downstream tooling imports. Two filters:

     """Post-process YOLO column detections on a tiled-inference output. Two
     filters, both shape-based (no model needed):

       (1) Aspect-ratio filter ‚ÄĒ drop detections with max(w,h)/min(w,h) > 2.5.
           Real columns are square-to-2:1. Anything taller-than-3√ó is text.
       (2) Cross-tile merge ‚ÄĒ IoU-aware NMS across the full canvas at 
     iou_thr=0.30
           (looser than YOLO's default 0.50) so the seam-ghost half-overlapping
           duplicate (small displaced bbox next to a real column) gets merged.

     Usage:
         from scripts.postprocess_detections import filter_detections
         detections = filter_detections(detections,
                                         max_aspect=2.5, nms_iou=0.30)
     """

     Implementation: standard NMS (sort by confidence, greedy IoU suppression),
     plus a pre-filter on aspect ratio. ~60 lines, no heavyweight deps (numpy +
     nothing else). Sketched as a module so the consumer imports it; not wired
     into this repo's training scripts.

     E. No changes to the orphan scrub (revised stance)

     The earlier plan iteration proposed deleting _is_orphan_label. Drop that
     work ‚ÄĒ the FPs in question come from inference-time model output on real
     plans, not from the synthetic dataset's label-on-blank-paper issue. The
     orphan scrub is unrelated to these four categories. Leave it.

     Reused, not reinvented

     - _bbox_overlaps_any / _padded_rect (:584-602) ‚ÄĒ already the chokepoint
     used by structure footprint registration and the column gate. Re-used by
     draw_small_text_decoys for the decoy-vs-column overlap test.
     - _paste_rotated_text (:251) ‚ÄĒ re-used for rotated decoys, no new
     rotation primitive.
     - _text_centered (:427) ‚ÄĒ re-used for non-rotated decoy placement.
     - _load_regular_font (:230) ‚ÄĒ same font path as existing decoys.
     - _place_edge_flanking_columns (:1055) ‚ÄĒ unchanged; stair fix is the
     caller's budget logic, not the helper.

     Files modified

     - generate_column.py ‚ÄĒ edits A (stair flanking caller) + B (new
     draw_small_text_decoys + COLUMN_MIMIC_TOKEN_POOL constant near the
     other pools at :181-204 + one call line in generate_image) + C
     (five sub-edits for cls 4 coverage: grid-loop weights at :1904, TP
     picker at :979, _make_unshaded stroke at :385, cls 4 interior text
     in place_column at :467, bubble-size sanity check at :1547).
     - scripts/postprocess_detections.py ‚ÄĒ new file, ~60 lines.

     Verification

     1. Syntax: python3 -c "import ast; 
     ast.parse(open('generate_column.py').read())"
     and same for the new script.
     2. Smoke generation: python3 generate_column.py --clean --out /tmp/colsmoke
     --canvases 2.
     3. Stair flanking sanity (Cat¬†3): write a one-off in /tmp that calls
     maybe_draw_stair_3wall 200 times and asserts the labels list per call
     has ‚Č§ 3 + corner-cols. Should be 0/200 violations.
     4. Decoy non-overlap (Cat 2/4): adapt /tmp/check_orphans.py style ‚ÄĒ for
     each tile in /tmp/colsmoke, assert no YOLO label bbox covers a small-text
     decoy centroid. Should be 0 violations (the col_rects gate ensures this).
     5. Visual eyeball: open ~10 human_check/ tiles from the smoke run.
     Confirm: (a) stairs no longer have a vertical strip of flanking columns;
     (b) small isolated letters and vertical "RCB3"-style tokens appear at
     column-pixel sizes WITHOUT red bboxes around them; (c) unshaded round
     columns (cls¬†4) appear in structure-adjacent positions (corners /
     edges of stairs, lifts, openings, cores) and at variable stroke
     weights (1‚Äď3 px), with ~55% carrying a small interior label.
     6. Post-processing: unit-test filter_detections on a synthetic input:
     a 30√ó80 detection (aspect 2.67) is dropped; two boxes with IoU 0.35 are
     merged into the higher-confidence one.
     7. User retrains (train_continue.py), then re-runs inference on the
     same real plan, then re-classifies the FP categories. Expected: Cat 1
     eliminated by post-processing; Cat 2/4 reduced because the model has now
     seen small-text-not-column examples; Cat 3 dense stair strip gone.

     Out of scope

     - Training (user does this manually).

‚óŹ Auto mode lets Claude handle permission prompts automatically ‚ÄĒ Claude
  checks each tool call for risky actions and prompt injection before 
  executing. Actions Claude identifies as safe are executed, while 
  actions Claude identifies as risky are blocked and Claude may try a 
  different approach. Ideal for long-running tasks. Sessions are 
  slightly more expensive. Claude can make mistakes that allow harmful 
  commands to run, it's recommended to only use in isolated 
  environments. Shift+Tab to change mode.

‚óŹ User approved Claude's plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/woolly-floating-llama.md ¬∑ /plan to edit
     Plan ‚ÄĒ Repair findings 1 & 2 from the code-review, restore the Cat 5 fix

     Context

     The earlier combined plan (Cat 1-5) was implemented and verified, but a
     3-angle high-effort code review surfaced two critical regressions in
     that implementation. Both were empirically reproduced; together they
     silently undo the Cat 5 unshaded-round fix and corrupt the new small-
     text decoys.

     Finding #1 ‚ÄĒ _make_unshaded 1-px stroke is silently scrubbed

     _make_unshaded (generate_column.py:385-394) now picks
     random.choice([1, 2, 2, 3]) as the stroke width. The orphan scrub
     _is_orphan_label (:632-653) samples at offset
     hx = bw/2 - LABEL_PAD - 1 = size/2 - 1 ‚ÄĒ exactly 1 pixel inside the
     1-px outline at radius size/2.

     Empirically verified for cls 4 / 5 / 6 at every size band: all 5 sample
     pixels read (255, 255, 255) ‚Üí scrub returns True ‚Üí label dropped.
     Outcome: ~25 % of every unshaded shape silently loses its YOLO label.
     Cls 4 sizes 24-27 (no interior text by gate size >= 28) regress in
     ~5 % of cases guaranteed; cls 4 size ‚Č• 28 without interior text regress
     in ~11 % of cases. This is the exact FN the Cat 5 work was meant to
     eliminate ‚ÄĒ net effect: same-or-worse than the pre-change baseline.

     Finding #2 ‚ÄĒ draw_small_text_decoys gate misses main-grid columns

     draw_small_text_decoys (:1620+) gates candidates with
     _bbox_overlaps_any(cand, col_rects). But col_rects only ever receives
     structure footprints + structure-edge column rects. The main grid
     loop (:1957-1987) appends to col_bboxes, placed, and labels ‚ÄĒ but
     never to col_rects.

     With hundreds of grid columns per canvas and 10-25 decoys per active
     canvas, decoy text frequently lands on top of a labelled grid column:
     - White-fill ink overlays the column outline ‚Üí orphan-scrub samples may
     shift / labels become inconsistent.
     - The column is now visually a "column with random letter inside" ‚ÄĒ a
     noise pattern that contradicts the cls-4-interior-text positive signal.

     Approach

     Two small, targeted edits ‚ÄĒ no new code.

     Fix 1 ‚ÄĒ restore 2-px stroke floor

     generate_column.py:385-394:

     def _make_unshaded(fn):
         """...stroke randomised across 2-3 px so the model sees a small range
         of line weights without falling below the orphan-scrub's 1-px inset
         sampling. The 1-px option was removed because the scrub samples at
         radius (size/2 - 1), one pixel INSIDE a 1-px outline, and would
         silently drop ~25 % of unshaded labels."""
         def _draw(draw, cx, cy, s, _fill, outline, lw):
             w = random.choice([2, 2, 2, 3])
             return fn(draw, cx, cy, s, (255, 255, 255), outline, w)
         return _draw

     Preserves the Cat 5 intent (variable stroke width) without breaking the
     scrub. 75 % of unshaded shapes draw at 2 px (matches the original
     behaviour); 25 % draw at 3 px (new ‚ÄĒ gives the model a slightly thicker
     variant to learn). Both pass the scrub at every size in
     ROUND_MIN_SIZE..ROUND_MAX_SIZE and COL_MIN_SIZE..COL_MAX_SIZE.

     Fix 2 ‚ÄĒ main grid columns also populate col_rects

     generate_column.py:1957-1987, immediately after the successful grid
     placement at line 1984-1987, add one line:

     bbox, yolo_cls = place_column(draw, cx, cy, cls, size)
     placed.append((cx, cy))
     col_bboxes.append((cx, cy, bbox))
     col_rects.append(_padded_rect(bbox))   # NEW: expose to late drawers
     labels.append(_yolo_label(bbox, yolo_cls))

     Update the col_rects declaration comment (:1920-1926) to drop the
     "structure footprints only" wording ‚ÄĒ it now also tracks main-grid
     columns added in this loop. The struct_rects = list(col_rects) snapshot
     on :1955 is taken BEFORE the grid loop runs, so the loop's own gate is
     unchanged (still O(structures), still grid-vs-grid is geometrically
     impossible).

     Result: draw_small_text_decoys and any future late drawer that gates on
     col_rects will now refuse to overlap grid columns.

     Reused, not reinvented

     - _padded_rect (:584) ‚ÄĒ same helper used by every other site that
     appends to col_rects. Single chokepoint for the YOLO-label inflation.
     - _bbox_overlaps_any (:588) ‚ÄĒ unchanged; only its candidate-list
     input is now complete.
     - No new helpers, no new constants.

     Out of scope (deferred)

     Findings 3-6 from the review are real but lower-severity and not strictly
     needed to make Cat 5 work. They can be addressed in a follow-up:

     - #3 cls 4 interior text overflow at small sizes
     - #4 decoy activation rate 15 % ‚Üí 60 %
     - #5 rotated-text AABB underestimate
     - #6 'C2' / 'RC' appear in both pools (contradictory signal)
     - #7 cross_tile_nms input-order dependence when conf missing
     - #8 scripts/__init__.py missing

     Verification

     1. Syntax: python3 -c "import ast; 
     ast.parse(open('generate_column.py').read())".
     2. Empirical orphan-scrub regression test (the exact test that exposed
     finding #1): for every size in (24, 32, 42) and every stroke in
     (2, 3), draw an unshaded circle and confirm at least one of the 5
     scrub sample points lands on ink (RGB < ORPHAN_BG_THRESHOLD).
     3. Smoke regenerate: python3 generate_column.py --clean --out /tmp/colsmoke
     --canvases 2.
     4. Orphan-check on the smoke set: python3 /tmp/check_orphans.py ‚Üí
     expect orphans 0 (was already 0; this fix shouldn't regress it).
     5. Cls 4 coverage re-run: python3 /tmp/check_cls4_coverage.py ‚Üí
     expect cls 4 share ‚Čą 12 %, still reaches both structure-adjacent
     placements, AND now also expect total cls 4 labels to STAY equal to
     the drawn count (no scrub drops). Add an assertion: count cls 4
     place_column calls vs cls 4 labels surviving the scrub; difference
     must be 0 (was previously ~25 % of all unshaded shapes lost).
     6. Decoy-vs-grid-column collision test (new, for finding #2): hook
     draw_small_text_decoys to record each candidate's AABB; iterate over
     col_bboxes from the same canvas; assert no decoy AABB overlaps a
     placed grid column. Expect 0 collisions.
     7. Visual eyeball: open ~5 human_check/ tiles, confirm (a) unshaded
     shapes have visible 2-3 px outlines (not the previous thin/missing
     1-px option) and (b) no small text decoys overlay a labelled column.

     Files modified

     - generate_column.py ‚ÄĒ two edits: _make_unshaded body (line 385-394)
     and one new line + one comment update in generate_image (line

      "summary": "Dropping the 1-px stroke option removes training-data coverage

  scale.",
      "failure_scenario": "Real architectural drawings rendered at 1:400 or with
  high-res 1-bit scans produce ~1-px outlines on unshaded round columns. The 
  model never sees this stroke weight in training, so it FNs on those at 
  inference. The accepted trade-off (chosen over relaxing the orphan scrub) 
  leaves this coverage gap. A future fix could change `_is_orphan_label`'s 
  sample inset from `hx = bw/2 - LABEL_PAD - 1` to `hx = bw/2 - LABEL_PAD` (one 
  pixel outward, landing ON the ring), reinstating the 1-px stroke without scrub
  false-drops."
    },

      "file": "generate_column.py",

      "summary": "At SMALL_COL_PROB cls 5 sizes (12-20 px) with stroke=3, the 
  outline-only shape is visually near-solid and collapses with filled cls 0.",
      "failure_scenario": "SMALL_COL_PROB downsizes cls 5 to 12-20 px (line 
  1976). With random.choice([2,2,2,3]) yielding stroke=3 (25% chance), at 
  size=12 the inward stroke leaves only a 6x6 white interior in a 12x12 box. At 
  inference scale this reads as a small dark filled square, indistinguishable 
  from cls 0. YOLO class is still 0 so no label correctness issue, but the 
  unshaded-as-positive signal is partially undone at the smallest sizes. 
  Mitigation: bump the stroke=3 minimum size or downweight to [2,2,2,2,3] for 
  tiny shapes."
    },

      "file": "generate_column.py",
      "line": 1921,
      "summary": "The col_rects declaration comment now describes 
  mixed-semantics storage but doesn't make the padded/unpadded asymmetry 
  explicit enough.",
      "failure_scenario": "Future maintainer reading 'Structure footprints are 
  stored UNPADDED' may not realize that column entries (both structure-edge and 
  main-grid) are stored PADDED. If they refactor a new helper that assumes 
  uniform padding, they'd either double-pad column entries or strip padding from
  structure entries, breaking the `_bay_is_clear` / `_square_overlaps_cols` 
  contracts. Fix: rephrase to 'Column rects (structure-edge + main-grid): PADDED
  by LABEL_PAD. Structure footprints: UNPADDED.' as two parallel bullets."

  misalign.",
      "failure_scenario": "col_bboxes uses None placeholders on skipped 
  intersections (lines 1965, 1985) to preserve the grid index. col_rects only 
  gets entries on successful placements AND already has a structure-rect prefix 
  from before the loop. Today only draw_small_text_decoys reads col_rects

  is added that naturally writes `col_rects[vi*nh+hi]` to look up a column's

  loop), it would silently misalign by ~20% (the sparse-skip rate) plus the 
  structure-rect prefix offset, leading to partition walls/labels pointing at 
  wrong intersections. Mitigation: a one-line comment above the new append 
  clarifying col_rects is set-semantics only, never index-aligned with 
  col_bboxes."

‚óŹ Updated plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†/plan to preview

‚óŹ User approved Claude's plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/woolly-floating-llama.md ¬∑ /plan to edit
     Plan ‚ÄĒ External column labels + 2-3 cap on opening/lift flanking

     Context

     User feedback on a fresh dataset sweep surfaced two wrong patterns that
     this
     plan addresses:

     1. "Text should not be INSIDE the column ‚ÄĒ it belongs OUTSIDE, either
     slanted or flat." This directly invalidates the cls 4 interior text
     block added in the prior Cat 5 pass (place_column lines 506-514). On
     real plans the column label (e.g. C2, √ė1130) sits adjacent to the
     column with a small offset and is frequently rotated 45¬į or 90¬į,
     matching the bay-edge / wall-thickness annotation convention. The
     interior-text block trained the model on a layout that does not occur
     in production.
     2. "Near an opening or stairs there should be 2 or max 3 columns."
     The stair-flanking budget was already thinned to 1-3 in the prior pass.
     Openings (max_cols=4 per edge √ó 4 edges = up to¬†16) and lifts
     (max_cols=5 per edge √ó 4 edges = up to¬†20) still drop dense strips.
     The earlier real-plan FPs in Image #3 (vertical stair-edge strip) will
     re-appear on openings / lifts unless those structures get the same
     thin-flanking treatment.

     User answers to clarification:
     - Lifts: same 2-3 cap as openings.
     - External labels: cover all column classes, ~40 % of grid columns.

     Approach

     Three small, targeted edits to generate_column.py ‚ÄĒ all reuse existing
     helpers; no new constants beyond using COLUMN_LABEL_POOL (already exists
     at :181-189).

     Edit 1 ‚ÄĒ Delete the cls 4 interior-text block

     place_column (:503-514). Remove the if cls == 4 and size >= 28 and 
     random.random() < 0.55: block and its docstring justification. The
     post-deletion if shape_name is not None body becomes:

     shape_name = _CLS_TO_SHAPE.get(cls)
     if shape_name is not None:
         bbox, _ = _SHAPE[shape_name](draw, cx, cy, size, fill, outline, 2)
         return bbox, 0

     The cls 4 bubble-confusion problem the interior text was trying to fix is
     now addressed by Edit 2 (external labels) and the existing size gap
     (bubbles 118-138 px diameter vs cls 4 24-42 px).

     Edit 2 ‚ÄĒ New draw_column_labels drawer

     A new late drawer that adds an unlabelled external text annotation
     adjacent to ~40 % of grid columns. Mirrors real-plan column-label style.

     Placement: pick a side (top/bottom/left/right), small gap of
     ~6 px from the column's outer edge. Try up to 4 sides, take the first
     that doesn't overlap col_rects (or skip the column if all 4 are
     blocked).

     Rotation: random.choice([0, 45, 90]) ‚ÄĒ flat, slanted, vertical.

     Token: derived from existing COLUMN_LABEL_POOL (:181-189). The
     multi-line entries ("C2\n800√ó800") are split on \n so the external
     form can be the short tag alone ("C2") or the full label, randomly.

     Font: regular weight, 14-22 px sz ‚ÄĒ distinguishable from column ink.

     Sketch:

     def draw_column_labels(img, draw, col_bboxes, col_rects, gc):
         """Add small external text labels next to ~40 % of grid columns,
         rotated 0/45/90¬į. Replaces the broken cls 4 interior-text approach
         with the real-plan convention: column tag sits ADJACENT, not inside.
         Not bbox'd ‚ÄĒ these are unlabelled, like every other text decoy."""
         for entry in col_bboxes:
             if entry is None:
                 continue
             cx, cy, bbox = entry
             if random.random() > 0.40:
                 continue
             raw   = random.choice(COLUMN_LABEL_POOL)
             token = raw if random.random() < 0.5 else raw.split("\n")[0]
             sz    = random.randint(14, 22)
             font  = _load_regular_font(sz)
             angle = random.choice([0, 45, 90])
             for side in random.sample(("top", "bottom", "left", "right"), 4):
                 tx, ty, cand = _label_placement(bbox, side, sz, token, angle)
                 if not _bbox_overlaps_any(cand, col_rects):
                     if angle == 0:
                         _text_centered(draw, tx, ty, token, gc, font)
                     else:
                         _paste_rotated_text(img, tx, ty, token,
                                              font, gc, angle=angle)
                     break

     _label_placement is a tiny inline helper that returns the centre
     position and a conservative AABB given the side, font size, token
     length, and rotation. Rotated text's bounding box is approximated as
     the diagonal envelope (max(tw, sz) square) for 45¬į, and (sz, tw)
     swapped for 90¬į.

     Call site in generate_image, after the main grid loop and
     before draw_internal_partitions so partition lines avoid the
     new label rectangles via the existing col_rects gate:

     draw_column_labels(img, draw, col_bboxes, col_rects, gc)

     To keep partitions from being drawn through the new labels, the
     label's footprint is also appended to col_rects after a successful
     draw ‚ÄĒ same pattern the structure-footprint fix established.

     Edit 3 ‚ÄĒ Thin opening and lift flanking to 2-3 total

     Same pattern as the existing stair fix (maybe_draw_stair_3wall
     :1306-1322). Two call sites get the same treatment:

     maybe_draw_opening_big (:1213-1217):
     # OLD: for each edge, max_cols=4 with 0.55 probability
     # NEW: total per-opening budget 2-3 across shuffled edges
     budget = random.randint(2, 3)
     edges  = list(_outer_edges(sx1, sy1, sx2, sy2))
     random.shuffle(edges)
     for _name, ex1, ey1, ex2, ey2, dx, dy in edges:
         if budget <= 0: break
         take = random.randint(1, min(2, budget))
         placed = _place_edge_flanking_columns(
             draw, ex1, ey1, ex2, ey2, dx, dy, col_rects, max_cols=take)
         labels.extend(placed)
         budget -= len(placed)

     maybe_draw_lift_chopped (:1437-1441): identical pattern,
     budget 2-3.

     Reused, not reinvented

     - COLUMN_LABEL_POOL (:181-189) ‚ÄĒ existing real-plan token pool;
     reused verbatim. No new constants needed.
     - _bbox_overlaps_any (:588) ‚ÄĒ gates external label candidates
     against col_rects (which now includes grid columns from the prior
     fix), so labels never overlap a labelled column.
     - _paste_rotated_text (:251) ‚ÄĒ already used by partitions /
     small-text decoys for vertical text; reused for 45¬į and 90¬į
     rotations. No new rotation primitive.
     - _text_centered (:427) ‚ÄĒ same dual-path anchor handling as
     every existing text site.
     - _load_regular_font (:230) ‚ÄĒ existing regular-weight font
     loader.
     - _outer_edges (:1002) + _place_edge_flanking_columns
     (:1055) ‚ÄĒ unchanged. Opening / lift fixes are caller-level budget
     changes only, matching the stair pattern.

     Files modified

     - generate_column.py ‚ÄĒ only file touched:
       - place_column (:503-514): delete cls 4 interior text block
       - new draw_column_labels function (placed near draw_small_text_decoys)
       - one call line in generate_image (after grid loop, before partitions)
       - maybe_draw_opening_big (:1213-1217): replace per-edge flanking
     with budget 2-3 shuffled-edges pattern
       - maybe_draw_lift_chopped (:1437-1441): same budget pattern as
     opening

     Verification

     1. Syntax: python3 -c "import ast; 
     ast.parse(open('generate_column.py').read())".
     2. Smoke gen: python3 generate_column.py --clean --out /tmp/colsmoke 
     --canvases 2.
     3. Orphan check: python3 /tmp/check_orphans.py ‚Üí expect orphans 0.
     Critical: the new labels MUST be gated correctly so no labelled
     column has external text overlaying it past _bbox_overlaps_any's
     reach.
     4. Opening / lift flanking caps: reuse /tmp/check_stair_flanking.py
     pattern, adapted to call maybe_draw_opening_big and
     maybe_draw_lift_chopped. Assert per-opening / per-lift edge-flanking
     count ‚Č§¬†3. Should be 0 violations over 200 iterations each.
     5. External-label / column-non-overlap test: hook
     draw_column_labels, capture each placed label's AABB, iterate over
     the canvas's col_bboxes, assert no label AABB overlaps any column
     bbox. Should be 0 collisions.
     6. Visual eyeball: open ~5 human_check/ tiles and confirm:
       - No cls 4 column has text INSIDE the ring.
       - ~40 % of grid columns have a small text fragment adjacent to them
     (flat, slanted, or vertical), and that fragment is NOT bbox'd.
       - Openings and lifts no longer show dense vertical strips of
     flanking columns ‚ÄĒ at most 2-3 per structure.

     Out of scope

     - Findings #3-#8 from the prior code-review still deferred.
     - Geometry-table reference block at module top (kept untouched per
     standing user preference).
     - The 1-px-stroke training-data gap (deliberately accepted in the
     previous repair).
     - Labelling structure-edge or corner columns externally (only grid
     columns get external labels for this pass; covers the bulk of column
     count without complicating the structure drawers).

      1696 +def _label_placement(bbox, side, sz, token, angle, gap=6):   
      1697 +    """Return (cx, cy, cand_aabb) for an external column labe
           +l placed on the                                              
      1698 +    given `side` of `bbox` with a small `gap`. `cand_aabb` is
           + a conservative                                              
      1699 +    AABB used to gate against `col_rects` ‚ÄĒ overestimated for
           + 45¬į rotations                                               
      1700 +    (we use a square envelope of `max(tw, sz)` instead of sol
           +ving the exact                                               
      1701 +    rotated rect)."""                                        
      1702 +    x1, y1, x2, y2 = bbox                                    
      1703 +    tw = sz * max(1, len(token))                             
      1704 +    if side == "top":                                        
      1705 +        cx = (x1 + x2) // 2                                  
      1706 +        cy = y1 - gap - sz // 2                              
      1707 +    elif side == "bottom":                                   
      1708 +        cx = (x1 + x2) // 2                                  
      1709 +        cy = y2 + gap + sz // 2                              
      1710 +    elif side == "left":                                     
      1711 +        cx = x1 - gap - tw // 2                              
      1712 +        cy = (y1 + y2) // 2                                  
      1713 +    else:  # right                                           
      1714 +        cx = x2 + gap + tw // 2                              
      1715 +        cy = (y1 + y2) // 2                                  
      1716 +    if angle == 0:                                           
      1717 +        cand_w, cand_h = tw, sz                              
      1718 +    elif angle == 90:                                        
      1719 +        cand_w, cand_h = sz, tw                              
      1720 +    else:  # 45 ‚ÄĒ diagonal envelope                          
      1721 +        side_env = max(tw, sz)                               
      1722 +        cand_w = cand_h = side_env                           
      1723 +    cand = (cx - cand_w // 2, cy - cand_h // 2,              
      1724 +            cx + cand_w // 2, cy + cand_h // 2)              
      1725 +    return cx, cy, cand                                      
      1726 +                                                             
      1727 +

  Edit 1 ‚ÄĒ place_column (:503-506): deleted the cls 4 interior-text block. cls 4

  (after grid loop, before partitions): ~40 % of grid columns get an adjacent
  text label, rotated uniformly across 0¬į / 45¬į / 90¬į, tried on each of the 4
  sides until one fits, gated against col_rects and its own footprint registered
  to prevent partition lines bisecting it. Tokens drawn from COLUMN_LABEL_POOL
  (existing), with half-the-time short tag (C2) and half-the-time full label

  max_cols=4 / max_cols=5 with the same shuffled-edges budget-2-3 pattern as
